**Changelog v4.2** (01/08/2026):
- ‚úÖ **[BLOCKING QUESTIONS SOLO DEV]** Added mandatory section: Blocking Questions for Doubts (Solo Dev)
- ‚úÖ Doubts are BLOCKING: clarify now or debug alone at 2AM later
- ‚úÖ AI MUST warn clear risks (wrong assumptions = debugging alone at dawn, no team to save you)
- ‚úÖ Pragmatic solo process: Direct questions ‚Üí Practical options ‚Üí Document in simple DECISIONS.md (no bureaucracy)
- ‚úÖ 6 types of blocking doubts: Requirements (you're the PO), Architecture (KISS vs patterns), Integration (you maintain everything), Data (corruption is nightmare), Behavior (production bugs), Tests (you're the QA)
- ‚úÖ Explicit solo trade-off: 5min asking vs 4h fixing alone + tests + deploy + rollback
- ‚úÖ Complete pragmatic examples: CPF validation, Cache system (solo cost-benefit analysis, no overengineering)
- ‚úÖ Quick solo checklist (2min): Total clarity? Edge cases? YAGNI check? Future-you check? Sleep-at-night check?
- ‚úÖ Realistic consequences: Solo midnight debugging, expensive rework (6h vs 2h), silent bugs, solo tech debt, momentum loss
- ‚úÖ Solo success metrics: Sleep 8h/night, rework <10%, clean commits, bugs <1/month, constant velocity
- ‚úÖ Solo golden rule: "5min asking now vs 4h debugging alone at 2AM. Choose wisely."
- ‚úÖ Pragmatism: Start simple (MVP), abstract on 3rd time, prefer composition, cache only if performance is REAL problem

- ‚úÖ Prohibition 5: AI MUST try 5 alternatives before giving up (AI is your only "colleague")
- ‚úÖ 5 solo alternatives: (1) Reread your docs, (2) Ask you, (3) Search online, (4) Other AIs, (5) Investigate your code
- ‚úÖ Pragmatic interruption protocol: Context, what's done, what's missing, why stopped
- ‚úÖ Honesty that protects your sleep: "Works BUT has risk X" (warn before you deploy)
- ‚úÖ Pragmatic focus: Ship MVP first, improve later (without stalling with secondary)
- ‚úÖ Solo mindset: "Protect your sleep" - AI's sincerity = your only backup
- ‚úÖ Checklist of 5 items before saying "I can't"

## ü§ù Human-AI Interaction Guide: Main Steps for Software Development

**CRITICAL NOTICE**: The artificial intelligence MUST be notified about the main steps to correctly perform the software development process. The interaction between human beings and artificial intelligence MUST follow this flow:

### üìã Complete Development Process (8 Steps)

#### **Step 1: Choose and Read 100% of the Protocol**
- Choose one of the simplicity protocols (example: Simplicity Protocol 3)
- The AI MUST read **100% of the chosen protocol**
- This is the **first mandatory step** before any action
- Without complete reading, the AI will not have the necessary methodological context

#### **Step 2: Study 100% of Documentation and Code**
After the protocol has been 100% read:
1. **Documentation**: The AI MUST study **100% of the project documentation**
2. **Source Code**: If there is code, the AI MUST study **100% of the code** (if not already read)
3. **Git History**: The AI MUST read the entire project history with:
   ```bash
   git log --all --stat --graph --decorate
   ```
4. **Tests**: The AI MUST study and investigate algorithm behavior by running test codes from the `tests/` folder

**Recommended order**: Protocol ‚Üí Documentation ‚Üí Git Log ‚Üí Code ‚Üí Tests

#### **Step 3: Document Tasks in docs/TASKS.md**
**Scenario A - If `docs/TASKS.md` does NOT exist:**
1. Ask the AI to document your tasks in `docs/ORIGINAL-TASKS.md`
2. The AI will use the protocol to organize tasks from `docs/ORIGINAL-TASKS.md` ‚Üí `docs/TASKS.md`
3. If you already have the requirements, place them in `docs/ORIGINAL-TASKS.md`
4. If you do NOT have the requirements, discuss with the AI what needs to be implemented
5. These requirements should be listed directly in `docs/TASKS.md`

**Scenario B - If `docs/TASKS.md` exists:**
1. The AI already has the structured task list
2. Proceed to Step 4

**üîë Importance**: Documenting features is essential to:
- Make the protocol more effective
- Ensure requirements are documented and remembered later
- Allow clear organization of all demands

#### **Step 4: Complete Tasks According to the Protocol**
1. With documentation read and tasks defined, ask the AI to complete the tasks
2. Execute **one task at a time**, following the simplicity protocol
3. **You do NOT need to choose which task**: The protocol's central rule is to solve:
   - Simplest tasks first
   - Tasks that other tasks depend on to be executed
   - Task/sprint/feature/requirement selection is **automatic**

#### **Step 5: Refine Requirements with Questions and Answers**
1. **Answer the questions** that the AI asks in each session
2. This allows refining the requirements
3. The AI will better understand what it should do
4. **Observe the protocol in action** at this stage
5. See your software being developed incrementally

**üéØ Bilateral relationship**: Client and AI learn from each other (student-teacher relationship)

#### **Step 6: Test User Experience (UX)**
1. The AI can perform **automated technical tests**
2. **You** need to conduct **user experience (UX) tests**
3. Until the user experience is satisfactory:
   - Provide details of your experience
   - Explain what you want to do
   - Continue refining until the AI gets it right, according to the simplicity protocol

**üîÅ Iterative cycle**: Test ‚Üí Feedback ‚Üí Refinement ‚Üí Test again

#### **Step 7: Final Verification - Mandatory Questions**
When the AI signals that it has finished and that the program/application has been completed, **ALWAYS** ask to challenge the AI's assumptions:

**Question 1 (Mandatory):**
```
‚ùì "What does this program do?"
```
- The AI will give a description of how the program/application turned out

**Question 2 (Mandatory):**
```
‚ùì "And do you GUARANTEE that the program does ALL of this?"
```
- This question will reveal if the AI actually managed to perform the requested activities
- It will reveal if the AI is being sincere and honest in what it says

**üö® STRONGLY RECOMMENDED**: Ask these two questions after the AI signals completion

**After the two questions, ask the AI to:**
1. Install dependencies
2. Run all tests
3. Finalize pending sprints
4. Check for orphaned code (unused code)
5. Analyze if refactoring was successful
6. Get organized and follow the simplicity protocol
7. Create a **detailed action plan** with specific stages
8. Record **step by step** in the action plan what needs to be done to get organized
9. Divide into clear phases/stages

#### **Step 8: Software Completion**
‚úÖ **Success criteria**:
1. All requirements are implemented
2. There are no known bugs
3. User experience (UX) tests are a success
4. All automated tests pass
5. Code is organized and documented

üéâ **Congratulations, your software is finished!**

---

### üìä Human-AI Interaction Checklist

**Before starting to program:**
- [ ] ‚úÖ I chose a simplicity protocol (1, 2, or 3)
- [ ] ‚úÖ AI read 100% of the chosen protocol
- [ ] ‚úÖ AI studied 100% of existing documentation
- [ ] ‚úÖ AI read entire Git history (`git log --all --stat`)
- [ ] ‚úÖ AI studied 100% of source code (if it exists)
- [ ] ‚úÖ AI executed tests from `tests/` folder to understand behavior
- [ ] ‚úÖ Tasks documented in `docs/TASKS.md` or `docs/ORIGINAL-TASKS.md`

**During development:**
- [ ] ‚úÖ AI is completing tasks one at a time
- [ ] ‚úÖ AI automatically chooses simple tasks or tasks with dependencies
- [ ] ‚úÖ I am answering AI questions to refine requirements
- [ ] ‚úÖ I am observing the protocol in action
- [ ] ‚úÖ I am testing user experience (UX)
- [ ] ‚úÖ I am providing detailed UX feedback

**Final verification:**
- [ ] ‚úÖ Asked: "What does this program do?"
- [ ] ‚úÖ Asked: "And do you GUARANTEE that the program does ALL of this?"
- [ ] ‚úÖ AI installed all dependencies
- [ ] ‚úÖ AI executed all tests successfully
- [ ] ‚úÖ AI finalized all pending sprints
- [ ] ‚úÖ AI checked for orphaned code
- [ ] ‚úÖ AI analyzed refactoring success
- [ ] ‚úÖ AI created detailed action plan
- [ ] ‚úÖ All requirements implemented
- [ ] ‚úÖ No known bugs
- [ ] ‚úÖ UX tests successful

---

### üéØ Golden Rules of Human-AI Interaction

1. **üìñ Complete Reading**: AI MUST read 100% of the protocol before any action
2. **üîç Deep Study**: AI MUST study docs, git log, code, and tests before implementing
3. **üìù Clear Documentation**: All tasks MUST be in `docs/TASKS.md`
4. **üéØ Incremental Focus**: One task at a time, from simplest to most complex
5. **üí¨ Active Communication**: Questions and answers continuously refine requirements
6. **üß™ Continuous Testing**: AI tests technically, user tests experience (UX)
7. **‚úÖ Final Verification**: Always ask the 2 mandatory questions at the end
8. **üéâ Clear Criteria**: Finished software = requirements + no bugs + perfect UX

---

### ‚ö†Ô∏è Important Warnings

**For the AI:**
- üö´ **NEVER** skip complete protocol reading
- üö´ **NEVER** start coding without studying documentation, git log, and code
- üö´ **NEVER** assume you understood everything without asking questions
- üö´ **NEVER** say you finished without guaranteeing EVERYTHING works
- ‚úÖ **ALWAYS** be sincere and honest, even if it temporarily displeases
- ‚úÖ **ALWAYS** answer the 2 mandatory questions with complete honesty

**For the User:**
- üìã **ALWAYS** document requirements in `docs/TASKS.md` or `docs/ORIGINAL-TASKS.md`
- üí¨ **ALWAYS** answer AI questions to refine requirements
- üß™ **ALWAYS** test user experience (UX) personally
- ‚ùì **ALWAYS** ask the 2 mandatory questions at the end
- üîç **ALWAYS** verify if the AI really delivered what it promised

## üéØ Why Does Simplicity 3 Exist?

### Project Context
- üë§ **Solo Developer**: You program alone (without a team)
- üöÄ **Production**: Application has real users depending on it
- ‚ö†Ô∏è **Critical**: Bugs affect users, downtime has impact
- üìà **Evolutive**: Long-term project, not a prototype

### Why NOT Simplicity 1?
‚ùå **Simplicity 1** is **insufficient for production**:
- ‚ùå No security checklist ‚Üí Vulnerabilities can go to production
- ‚ùå No CI/CD automation ‚Üí Manual validation = human errors
- ‚ùå No rollback plan ‚Üí If it breaks in production, you're debugging alone
- ‚ùå No profiling ‚Üí Performance degrades without you noticing
- ‚ùå Basic documentation ‚Üí You forget complex decisions after 3 months

**Real Risk**: Simple application today = giant technical debt in 6 months.

### Why NOT Simplicity 2?
‚ùå **Simplicity 2** has **team overhead** unnecessary for a solo developer:
- ‚ùå **Peer Code Review** (Step 9.5) ‚Üí You have no peers
- ‚ùå **Formal Sprint Retrospectives** (Step 13.5) ‚Üí Overkill for one person
- ‚ùå **Formal ADRs** (Step 11.5) ‚Üí Can be simplified to decision notes
- ‚ùå **Accessibility WCAG** (Step 8.5) ‚Üí Only if the app is public/accessible
- ‚ùå **API Documentation Sphinx** (Step 6.6) ‚Üí Docstrings are sufficient

**Real Problem**: Bureaucracy consumes development time without real gain for a solo developer.

### ‚úÖ Simplicity 3 - Hybrid Solution

**Philosophy**: **Production security and automation** WITHOUT team overhead.

**Formula**:
```
Simplicity 3 = Simplicity 1 Base (13 steps)
                 + 3 MANDATORY production steps (Security, CI/CD, Rollback)
                 + 3 pragmatic OPTIONAL steps (Matrix, Profiling, ADR Notes)
                 = 16-19 total steps
```

**Additional MANDATORY Steps** (vs Simplicity 1):
1. ‚≠ê **Step 6.5: OWASP Security Checklist** - CRITICAL for production
2. ‚≠ê **Step 10.6: CI/CD Quality Gates** - Essential automation
3. ‚≠ê **Step 12.5: Rollback Plans** - Deployment safety

**Adapted OPTIONAL Steps** (when it makes sense):
4. üìä **Step 2.5: Decision Matrix** - When you have 10+ tasks to prioritize
5. ‚ö° **Step 10.5: Profiling** - For slow features (>1s)
6. üìù **Step 11.5: Decision Notes** - Simplified ADR (not formal)

**Removed from Simplicity 2** (don't make sense for solo dev):
- ‚ùå Step 9.5: Peer Code Review
- ‚ùå Step 13.5: Formal Sprint Retrospectives
- ‚ùå Step 8.5: Accessibility WCAG (unless app is public)
- ‚ùå Step 6.7: Formal API Documentation (docstrings are sufficient)

---

## üìä Protocol Comparison

| Aspect | Simplicity 1 | Simplicity 3 | Simplicity 2 |
|---------|----------------|----------------|----------------|
| **Steps** | 13 mandatory | 16 oblig + 3 opt | 13 oblig + 10 opt |
| **Scenario** | Prototypes/internal | **Solo in production** | Enterprise teams |
| **Security** | ‚ùå No | ‚úÖ OWASP mandatory | ‚úÖ OWASP mandatory |
| **CI/CD** | ‚ùå No | ‚úÖ Mandatory | ‚úÖ Mandatory |
| **Rollback** | ‚ùå No | ‚úÖ Mandatory | ‚úÖ Mandatory |
| **Code Review** | ‚ùå No | ‚ùå Solo | ‚úÖ Peers |
| **Retrospectives** | ‚ùå No | ‚ùå Solo | ‚úÖ Team |
| **Overhead** | Low | **Medium** | High |
| **Production** | ‚ùå Not recommended | ‚úÖ **IDEAL** | ‚úÖ Yes |
| **Time/Task** | ~2-3h | ~3-4h | ~4-6h |

---

## üéØ When to Use Simplicity 3?

### ‚úÖ Use Simplicity 3 IF:
- ‚úÖ You program **alone** (solo developer)
- ‚úÖ Application is or will go to **production**
- ‚úÖ You have **real users** depending on it (not a prototype)
- ‚úÖ Bugs have **impact** (downtime, data loss)
- ‚úÖ It's a **long-term project** (>6 months)
- ‚úÖ You need **security** (user data, LGPD/GDPR)
- ‚úÖ You want **automation** (CI/CD to not rely on memory)

### ‚ùå DO NOT use Simplicity 3 IF:
- ‚ùå Disposable prototype/POC ‚Üí Use **Simplicity 1**
- ‚ùå Single-use script ‚Üí Use **Simplicity 1**
- ‚ùå Team of 2+ people ‚Üí Use **Simplicity 2** (has code review)
- ‚ùå Non-critical internal app ‚Üí Use **Simplicity 1**
- ‚ùå Learning/experimenting ‚Üí Use **Simplicity 1**

  - Step 6.5: OWASP Security Checklist (‚≠ê HIGH PRIORITY)
  - Step 10.6: CI/CD Quality Gates (‚≠ê HIGH PRIORITY)
  - Step 12.5: Rollback Plans (‚≠ê HIGH PRIORITY)
- ‚úÖ **PRAGMATIC OPTIONAL**:
  - Step 2.5: Decision Matrix (when 10+ tasks)
  - Step 10.5: Profiling and Optimization (slow features)
  - Step 11.5: Decision Notes (simplified ADR)
- ‚úÖ **REMOVED** (don't make sense for solo dev):
  - ‚ùå Peer Code Review (no peers)
  - ‚ùå Formal Sprint Retrospectives (overkill solo)
  - ‚ùå Accessibility WCAG (unless public)
  - ‚ùå Formal API Documentation (docstrings sufficient)
- ‚úÖ Detailed Rationale: Why not Simplicity 1 or 2
- ‚úÖ Comparative table of the 3 protocols
- ‚úÖ Total: 16 mandatory + 3 optional = 16-19 steps

## üéØ Core Philosophy

> "There will always be complex tasks to do, but also those that are more difficult and those that are easier. **I want you to always start with the easiest ones**."

**Principle**: From simple to complex, incremental, professional, and complete.

**NEW v3.0**: + **Production security and automation** without team overhead.

---

## üìù PHILOSOPHY OF MAXIMUM CLARITY: Universal Documentation (Solo)

> **FUNDAMENTAL FOR AIs HELPING SOLO DEVS**: Artificial intelligence MUST write all documentation, execution plans, action plans and TASKS.md **AS IF** you (the solo developer) would read it 3 months later, half asleep, trying to debug a ticking time bomb. This is a **mandatory mental technique** to protect your sleep and your sanity.

### üéØ Central Principle: "Write for your panicked future self"

**Mandatory Solo Mindset:**
```markdown
The AI must ASSUME that:
- ‚úÖ You will read this document 3 months later, without context
- ‚úÖ You will be debugging a ticking time bomb at 2 AM
- ‚úÖ You will NOT have anyone to help (you're alone)
- ‚úÖ You may have slept poorly and be confused
- ‚úÖ If it's not ultra-clear, YOU will lose hours debugging
- ‚úÖ Everything must be self-explanatory, practical and pragmatic
- ‚úÖ Your time is precious (you have to do EVERYTHING alone)
```

**Real Objective:**
```markdown
‚ùå NOT about actually being another developer
‚úÖ It's about using this ASSUMPTION as TECHNIQUE to improve clarity
‚úÖ Writing "for your future self" = Force better explanations
‚úÖ Writing "for emergency" = Force pragmatism
‚úÖ Result: Documentation that protects your sleep
```

### üìã Mandatory Application in 4 Areas

#### 1Ô∏è‚É£ Execution Plans (Code Step by Step + Pragmatism)

**How to write:**
```markdown
‚úÖ CORRECT (solo pragmatic):

**Execution Plan: Implement CPF validation**

**TL;DR (if you wake up scared at 2AM):**
- File: `src/validators/cpf.py`
- Function: `validate_cpf(cpf: str) -> bool`
- Test: `pytest tests/test_cpf.py -v`
- Deploy: `git commit && git push` (CI/CD automatic)
- If it breaks: `git revert [commit-id] && git push`

---

**Step 1: Create validation function (PRAGMATIC)**
- File: `src/validators/cpf.py`
- Name: `validate_cpf(cpf: str) -> bool`
- What it does: Takes CPF string, returns True/False
- PRAGMATIC implementation (no overengineering):
  1. Remove non-numeric characters (.-/)
  2. Check if it has exactly 11 digits
  3. Check if they are not all equal
  4. Calculate first check digit (modulo 11)
  5. Calculate second check digit (modulo 11)
  6. Compare digits
  
**‚ö†Ô∏è CAREFUL (solo pitfalls):**
- DON'T add complex logging (will cause production issues)
- DON'T call external APIs (OFAC, etc) here (timeout risks)
- DON'T try to be super-robust (80% functionality, ship it)
- IF you find edge case later ‚Üí add it to test, not code

**How to test fast (3 minutes):**
```bash
python3 -c "from src.validators.cpf import validate_cpf; print(validate_cpf('123.456.789-09'))"
# Should print: True or False
```

**Step 2: Add minimal viable tests**
- File: `tests/test_cpf.py`
- Framework: pytest (already installed)
- Minimal cases (no perfectionism):
  1. Valid CPF: "123.456.789-09" ‚Üí True
  2. Invalid CPF: "123.456.789-00" ‚Üí False
  3. Wrong size CPF: "123" ‚Üí False
- Command: `pytest tests/test_cpf.py -v`
- Time: 15 minutes (not more!)

**SOLO PRAGMATISM:** Don't do 50 tests, do 3 good ones. If it breaks, add test.

**Step 3: Integrate in endpoint (QUICK & DIRTY)**
- File: `src/routes/users.py`
- Minimal modification:
  ```python
  from src.validators.cpf import validate_cpf
  
  @app.route('POST /api/users')
  def create_user(request):
      cpf = request.json.get('cpf', '')
      if not validate_cpf(cpf):
          return {"error": "Invalid CPF"}, 400
      # rest of code...
  ```
- Manual test: `curl -X POST http://localhost:5000/api/users -d '{"cpf":"123.456.789-09"}'`

**PRAGMATISM:** 1 minute implementation, 2 minutes testing. If you need to improve later, it's documented.

---

‚ùå WRONG (overengineered for solo):

**Execution Plan: Implement CPF validation**
- Create function with distributed logging
- Add 50 compliance tests
- Integrate with multiple external APIs
- Implement circuit breaker + retry logic
(Perfect for team of 10. For solo? You'll never finish!)
```

- [ ] Create directory structure (5 min)

- [ ] Run first test (5 min)
- **Total: 25 minutes, not 2 hours!**

mkdir -p src/{models,routes,validators} tests

**Quick verification:**

```

# Windows
python -m venv venv
venv\Scripts\activate
```
**Verification:** Prompt has `(venv)` at the beginning

**Task 3: Install (minimum viable)**
File: `requirements.txt`
```
flask==3.0.0
pytest==7.4.3
```
```bash
pip install -r requirements.txt
```

---

**Completion criteria:**
- [ ] Structure created
- [ ] Environment active
- [ ] Dependencies installed
- **Real time: 25 minutes (not 2 hours!)**

**‚ö†Ô∏è IF YOU FIND PROBLEM:**
```
Error: "python3 not found"
Solution: Do you have Python installed? `python --version`

Error: "Permission denied"
Solution: Linux/Mac: `chmod +x script.sh` or use `sudo`
```

   - File: `tests/test_cpf.py`
   - Valid case, invalid case, edge case

   - Test: curl command

   ```bash

   ```

**Priority:** LOW (don't do now!)

---

**Session completion criteria:**
- [ ] Tasks completed in order
- [ ] Each task tested (don't move to next if it fails)
- [ ] Sleep: Can you sleep peacefully?
- **Estimated time: 1h (pragmatic, not optimistic!)**

---

‚ùå WRONG (burnout for solo):

(You CAN'T! Result: burnout in week 1)

#### 3Ô∏è‚É£ Documentation (Pragmatic README + DECISIONS.md)

**How to write:**
```markdown
‚úÖ CORRECT (solo pragmatic):

**README.md**

# Project [Name]

## Get Started Quick (3 minutes)

### Linux/Mac
\`\`\`bash
git clone [repo]
cd [project]
python3 -m venv venv
source venv/bin/activate
pip install -r requirements.txt
pytest tests/ -v
\`\`\`

### Windows
\`\`\`bash
git clone [repo]
cd [project]
python -m venv venv
venv\Scripts\activate
pip install -r requirements.txt
pytest tests/ -v
\`\`\`

## How Structure Works

```
src/
  validators/      ‚Üí Validations (CPF, email, etc)
  routes/          ‚Üí HTTP endpoints
  models/          ‚Üí Data classes
tests/
  test_cpf.py      ‚Üí CPF validation tests
docs/
  DECISIONS.md     ‚Üí Technical decisions (IMPORTANT!)
```

## DECISIONS.md (Your Treasure Map)

**Always start here** if you wake up confused at 2AM:

File: `docs/DECISIONS.md`

Contains:
- WHAT was decided
- WHY it was decided this way
- IF you want to change it later

Example:
```
# Decision: CPF Validation Algorithm

## Decided: Use module 11 algorithm
- Why: Brazilian standard, simple
- Alternative rejected: Regex (fragile)
- Documentation: [official link]
```

## Troubleshooting Solo (If it breaks)

**Test doesn't pass:**
1. `pytest tests/test_cpf.py -v` (see specific error)
2. If you don't understand error ‚Üí go to `DECISIONS.md` (may contain solution)
3. If still doesn't work ‚Üí `git log` (see previous commits)

**Deploy broke:**
1. `git log --oneline` (last 5 commits)
2. `git revert [problem-commit]`
3. `git push`
4. Sleep

**Can't remember something:**
1. Search in `DECISIONS.md`
2. Search in `.git log`
3. Search in `README.md`
4. BEFORE redoing

---

‚ùå WRONG (assumes too much):

**README.md**
## How to use
Clone and execute. See Javadocs.
(May work for team. For solo? You get lost!)
```

### ‚úÖ Maximum Clarity Checklist (Solo)

- [ ] Pragmatism: 80% functionality is enough?
```

### üéØ Golden Rule of Clarity (Solo)

> **"If you were not available to clarify doubts, would YOU YOURSELF (3 months later, confused, tired) be able to execute this plan just by reading the document? If NO, it's INCOMPLETE. Time spent documenting now = protected sleep later."**

**Practical example:**
```markdown
‚ùå BAD: "Add validation"
(What validation? Where? How?? You see this 3 months later... takes 30 min to remember)

(3 months later, you open this, understand in 1 minute, keep coding)
```

### üìö Philosophy Summary (Solo)

**Mindset:**
- ü§î "I write for YOU yourself, confused and tired, 3 months from now"
- üéØ This assumption is TECHNIQUE to protect your sleep
- ‚úÖ Goal: Pragmatic documentation that saves your life

**Application:**
- üìã Execution Plans: Step by step + pragmatism
- üéØ Action Plans: Realistic tasks + sleep protection
- üìñ Documentation: Clear README + DECISIONS.md
- ‚úÖ TASKS.md: Pragmatic map with rollback

**Result:**
- üíé Quality you can maintain alone
- üò¥ You can sleep peacefully
- ‚ö° If it breaks, fix in 5 minutes
- üöÄ Pragmatic speed (ship > theory)

---
## üîê SCRIPTS PHILOSOPHY: Security, Transparency, and Practicality (Solo)

> **FUNDAMENTAL FOR AIs HELPING SOLO DEVS**: When tasks require `sudo` or passwords, the artificial intelligence MUST create scripts instead of requesting passwords. The AI should NEVER ask for or receive sudo passwords (dangerous and not recommended). For solo devs, scripts are your defense against 2AM errors and sleepless nights. This approach makes interaction safer, more transparent, and pragmatic.

### üéØ Core Principle: Scripts that Protect Your Sleep

**Mandatory Rule:**
```markdown
‚ùå NEVER do:
- Ask for sudo password from user
- Request administrative credentials
- Execute privileged commands directly
- Assume you (AI) have root access
- Create scripts that break your production at 2AM

‚úÖ ALWAYS do:
- Create scripts for commands that need sudo
- Show complete code BEFORE execution
- Explain what each command does
- Document in DECISIONS.md the script purpose
- Include clear and tested rollback
- Let user execute and provide password when needed
```

### üìã Pragmatic Approach: When to Create Scripts (Solo)

**Decision based on complexity + risk:**

#### **Case 1: Few Commands (1-3 lines) ‚Üí NO script, JUST SHOW**

When there are only 1-3 simple sudo commands:

**Example - Quick Installation:**
```markdown
‚úÖ CORRECT (solo - just show):

To install Redis on your dev environment:

```bash
# Install Redis server (in-memory cache for sessions)
sudo apt install redis-server

# Start service
sudo systemctl start redis
```

You will be prompted to provide your sudo password.

Then test: `redis-cli ping` (should return PONG)
```

**When to use this approach:**
- ‚úÖ 1-2 simple sudo commands
- ‚úÖ Dev tool installation (not production)
- ‚úÖ Single quick operation
- ‚úÖ No impact on data or services

#### **Case 2: Multiple Commands or System-Breaking Risk ‚Üí CREATE script with Rollback**

When there are 3+ commands or operation could break your setup:

**Example - Complete Setup with Rollback:**
```markdown
‚úÖ CORRECT (solo - script with protection):

I created the `setup_redis.sh` script to configure Redis properly.

**‚ö†Ô∏è IMPORTANT: READ THE SCRIPT BEFORE EXECUTING!**

Please:
1. Open the file `setup_redis.sh` 
2. Read the comments above each line
3. Verify you're comfortable with what will be executed
4. Only then execute: `bash setup_redis.sh`

**Content of setup_redis.sh:**
```bash
#!/bin/bash
# setup_redis.sh - READ BEFORE EXECUTING
# Purpose: Install Redis with sensible configuration + safe rollback
# Rollback: Execute: bash setup_redis_rollback.sh
# Decision: DECISIONS.md#REDIS_CACHE_CHOICE (why Redis?)

set -e  # Exit if error
set -u  # Error if undefined variable

echo "=== Setup Redis (with safe rollback) ==="
echo "You will be prompted to provide your sudo password"
echo ""

# BACKUP: Save previous configuration (for rollback)
echo "Creating backup (safe rollback)..."
mkdir -p ~/.local/backups
[[ -f /etc/redis/redis.conf ]] && cp /etc/redis/redis.conf ~/.local/backups/redis.conf.backup.$(date +%s)

# Update package list to get recent versions
echo "Updating package list..."
sudo apt update

# Install Redis server (in-memory key-value database)
echo "Installing Redis server..."
sudo apt install -y redis-server

# Start Redis service
echo "Starting Redis service..."
sudo systemctl start redis

# Enable Redis to start automatically on boot
echo "Enabling Redis on boot..."
sudo systemctl enable redis

# Verify installation was successful
echo ""
echo "Checking installation..."
redis-cli --version

# CRITICAL test: Verify Redis works
echo "Testing Redis connection..."
if redis-cli ping | grep -q "PONG"; then
    echo "‚úÖ Redis working correctly!"
else
    echo "‚ùå ERROR: Redis did not respond"
    echo "Running automatic rollback..."
    bash setup_redis_rollback.sh
    exit 1
fi

echo ""
echo "‚úÖ Setup completed!"
echo "Redis is running. Test with: redis-cli ping"
echo ""
echo "To revert (if problems occur):"
echo "  bash setup_redis_rollback.sh"
```

**Rollback file - setup_redis_rollback.sh:**
```bash
#!/bin/bash
# setup_redis_rollback.sh - UNDO THE INSTALLATION
# Use if Redis is not working or causing problems

echo "=== Redis Rollback ==="
echo "Removing Redis..."

# Stop service
sudo systemctl stop redis || true
sudo systemctl disable redis || true

# Remove package
sudo apt remove -y redis-server redis-tools || true

# Restore previous configuration (if backup exists)
if [[ -f ~/.local/backups/redis.conf.backup.* ]]; then
    echo "Restoring previous configuration..."
    LATEST_BACKUP=$(ls -t ~/.local/backups/redis.conf.backup.* | head -n1)
    sudo cp "$LATEST_BACKUP" /etc/redis/redis.conf
fi

echo "‚úÖ Rollback completed"
echo "To reinstall, execute: bash setup_redis.sh"
```

**To execute (SAFE):**
```bash
chmod +x setup_redis.sh setup_redis_rollback.sh
bash setup_redis.sh

# If something goes wrong:
bash setup_redis_rollback.sh
```

You will provide your sudo password when the script requests it.
```

**When to use this approach:**
- ‚úÖ 3 or more sudo commands
- ‚úÖ Operations that could break your setup
- ‚úÖ Complex installations (Docker, Node versioning, etc)
- ‚úÖ Anything you want to revert quickly if problems occur
- ‚úÖ System that needs to stay working (You sleep on it!)

### üîç Transparency and Pragmatic Honesty

**The AI MUST always (solo dev):**

**1. Show complete code BEFORE execution**
```markdown
‚úÖ GOOD: "Here is the complete script. Please read before executing:"
```

**2. Explain what each command does in simple language**
```markdown
‚úÖ GOOD: Each line has a comment:
# Install Redis server (in-memory database for fast cache)
sudo apt install redis-server
```

**3. Ask the user to read the script**
```markdown
‚úÖ GOOD: "‚ö†Ô∏è IMPORTANT: Open setup.sh and read before executing"
```

**4. Be 100% honest about risks**
```markdown
‚úÖ GOOD: "This script will:
1. ‚úÖ Install Redis
2. ‚úÖ Start service
3. ‚ö†Ô∏è RISK: If Redis breaks your dev env, use rollback"
```

**5. Document decision reason in DECISIONS.md**
```markdown
‚úÖ GOOD: Script references DECISIONS.md:
# Decision: DECISIONS.md#REDIS_CACHE_CHOICE
# Why Redis? Fast, simple, better than Memcached for dev
```

### üõ°Ô∏è Security and Sleep Protection

**Why scripts (not passwords) save your sleep:**

```markdown
‚ùå DANGERS of requesting password + no rollback:
- üî¥ Redis breaks setup at 2AM, you can't revert
- üî¥ Don't even know how to remove what was installed
- üî¥ No backup of previous configuration
- üî¥ Lose time searching how to undo
- üî¥ You stay awake until 4AM trying to fix

‚úÖ BENEFITS of scripts with rollback:
- üü¢ Clear and documented installation
- üü¢ Rollback available if something breaks
- ÔøΩÔøΩ Simple command to return to previous state
- üü¢ You can sleep (script has plan B)
- üü¢ Decision reason documented in DECISIONS.md
- üü¢ Next time you understand what was done
```

### üí° Complete Practical Examples

#### **Example 1: Node Version Manager (Complete Script with Rollback)**

```bash
#!/bin/bash
# setup_nvm.sh - Install Node Version Manager
# Purpose: Allow multiple Node versions without conflicts
# Decision: DECISIONS.md#NVM_VS_SYSTEM_NODE
# Rollback: bash setup_nvm_rollback.sh

set -e

echo "=== Setup Node Version Manager ==="

# BACKUP
mkdir -p ~/.local/backups
cp -r ~/.nvm ~/.local/backups/nvm.backup.$(date +%s) 2>/dev/null || true

# Install NVM (Node Version Manager)
echo "Installing NVM..."
curl -o- https://raw.githubusercontent.com/nvm-sh/nvm/v0.39.0/install.sh | bash

# Reload bash config
export NVM_DIR="$HOME/.nvm"
[[ -s "$NVM_DIR/nvm.sh" ]] && \. "$NVM_DIR/nvm.sh"

# Install Node stable version
echo "Installing Node.js (LTS version)..."
nvm install --lts
nvm use --lts

# Verify installation
echo "Checking..."
node --version
npm --version

echo "‚úÖ NVM installed successfully!"
echo "To revert: bash setup_nvm_rollback.sh"
```

**Rollback:**
```bash
#!/bin/bash
# setup_nvm_rollback.sh

echo "=== NVM Rollback ==="
rm -rf ~/.nvm
echo "‚úÖ NVM removed"
echo "Reinstall with: bash setup_nvm.sh"
```

#### **Example 2: Docker Setup (Solo Friendly)**

```bash
#!/bin/bash
# setup_docker_solo.sh - Docker for local dev
# Purpose: Install Docker + add to your user
# Rollback: bash setup_docker_rollback.sh
# Note: After installation, logout/login

set -e

echo "=== Setup Docker (dev environment) ==="

# BACKUP
mkdir -p ~/.local/backups
groups > ~/.local/backups/groups.backup.$(date +%s)

# Remove old Docker (if exists)
echo "Removing old Docker..."
sudo apt remove -y docker docker-engine docker.io containerd runc 2>/dev/null || true

# Install dependencies
echo "Installing dependencies..."
sudo apt update
sudo apt install -y ca-certificates curl gnupg lsb-release

# Add Docker repository
echo "Adding Docker repository..."
sudo mkdir -p /etc/apt/keyrings
curl -fsSL https://download.docker.com/linux/ubuntu/gpg | sudo gpg --dearmor -o /etc/apt/keyrings/docker.gpg
echo "deb [arch=$(dpkg --print-architecture) signed-by=/etc/apt/keyrings/docker.gpg] https://download.docker.com/linux/ubuntu $(lsb_release -cs) stable" | sudo tee /etc/apt/sources.list.d/docker.list > /dev/null

# Install Docker
echo "Installing Docker..."
sudo apt update
sudo apt install -y docker-ce docker-ce-cli containerd.io docker-buildx-plugin docker-compose-plugin

# Add your user to docker group (avoids sudo for docker)
echo "Adding you to docker group..."
sudo usermod -aG docker $USER

# Start Docker
echo "Starting Docker..."
sudo systemctl start docker
sudo systemctl enable docker

# Test
echo "Testing Docker..."
sudo docker run hello-world > /dev/null && echo "‚úÖ Docker working!"

echo ""
echo "‚ö†Ô∏è IMPORTANT: Logout and login again to use docker without sudo"
echo "Or execute: newgrp docker"
echo ""
echo "Test with: docker run hello-world"
echo "To revert: sudo bash setup_docker_rollback.sh"
```

**Rollback:**
```bash
#!/bin/bash
# setup_docker_rollback.sh

echo "=== Docker Rollback ==="
sudo systemctl stop docker || true
sudo systemctl disable docker || true
sudo apt remove -y docker-ce docker-ce-cli containerd.io docker-buildx-plugin docker-compose-plugin || true
sudo groupdel docker || true
echo "‚úÖ Docker removed"
```

### ‚úÖ Solo Checklist for Safe Scripts

Before creating/presenting any script, the AI should verify:

```markdown
**Security:**
- [ ] Script does NOT request sudo password (user provides during execution)
- [ ] Each sudo command is commented and explained
- [ ] No destructive commands without warning
- [ ] Sensible file paths (doesn't overwrite important things)
- [ ] Rollback provided and tested

**Pragmatism:**
- [ ] Script solves REAL and immediate problem
- [ ] Installation is idempotent (running 2x is safe)
- [ ] Clear success test (docker run hello-world)
- [ ] Progress messages keep you informed
- [ ] Rollback is simple (one line, maximum)

**Transparency:**
- [ ] Complete code shown to user
- [ ] Comments in clear language
- [ ] General purpose documented in header
- [ ] Warned "READ BEFORE EXECUTING"
- [ ] Reference to DECISIONS.md for context

**Sleep Protection:**
- [ ] If 1-3 commands: Showed directly (no script)
- [ ] If ‚â•3 or risk: Created script with rollback
- [ ] Rollback is idempotent (running 2x doesn't break)
- [ ] You can revert to previous state in <1 minute
- [ ] DECISIONS.md documentation explains why
```

### üéì Benefits of This Philosophy (Solo)

**For Your Mental Health:**
```markdown
‚úÖ Scripts you can reuse later
‚úÖ Rollback prevents sleepless nights
‚úÖ You understand what was done 3 months later
‚úÖ Confidence to test new things
‚úÖ Protection against your own mistakes
```

**For Speed:**
```markdown
‚úÖ Automatic installation = more coding time
‚úÖ No copy-paste errors = fewer bugs
‚úÖ Fast rollback = less debugging time
‚úÖ Reusable scripts = don't reinvent wheel
‚úÖ Pragmatism = ship > perfection
```

**For Quality:**
```markdown
‚úÖ Decisions documented in DECISIONS.md
‚úÖ Consistent setup between dev and production
‚úÖ Errors easily identifiable
‚úÖ Simplified maintenance
‚úÖ Knowledge preserved in files
```

### üéØ Golden Rules (Solo)

**1. Security:**
> "NEVER request password. ALWAYS create script with rollback you can execute."

**2. Pragmatism:**
> "Script solves REAL problem. Rollback in <1 minute. You can sleep."

**3. Documentation:**
> "Clear code. DECISIONS.md explains why. Comments in plain language."

**4. Protection:**
> "I write AS IF you'll need to rollback at 2AM. Rollback is ready."

### üéØ Mandatory Professional Profile

#### üíº Essential Professional Characteristics

- ‚úÖ **Resilient**: Maintains quality even under pressure

### üôè Humility and Error Recognition

**Even being an elite senior, the AI MUST:**

**When Making Mistakes (it's human/expected):**
```markdown
‚úÖ **Admit error quickly**: "I made a mistake here, sorry"
‚úÖ **Explain the error**: "I assumed X when I should have confirmed Y"
‚úÖ **Correct immediately**: "I'll fix it now, estimated: 20 minutes"
‚úÖ **Learn**: "Next time, I'll [preventive action]"
‚úÖ **No excuses**: Don't blame tools, language, or client
‚úÖ **Solo**: Warn about risks BEFORE you lose hours debugging
```

**Example of Error Recognition (Solo):**
```markdown
üôè **Error Identified**

I implemented Redis caching without considering invalidation when 
a product is updated. This causes stale data for users.

**My failure**: I didn't ask about invalidation strategy.

**Why this is critical for you (solo dev)**:
- ‚ùå User sees wrong price, complains to support (you respond)
- ‚ùå Intermittent bug hard to reproduce (4h debugging)
- ‚ùå Possible lost sale (customer gives up)
- ‚ùå Product reputation affected
- ‚ùå **You're the only one debugging this at 3AM**

**Immediate correction**: 
- Implement invalidation via Redis pub/sub (30 min)
- Add test that verifies cache invalidates (15 min)
- Document caching policy in README (5 min)
- Add line to DECISIONS.md (5 min)

**Total**: 55 minutes to fix completely.

**Lesson learned**: Always ask about invalidation strategy 
when implementing any type of cache.

**Sorry about the error. Proceeding with the correction?**
```

**Posture of Humility**:
- ‚úÖ Acknowledge when unsure about something: "I'm not certain about X, I'll research it"
- ‚úÖ Accept feedback: "Good point, hadn't considered that"
- ‚úÖ Give credit: "That approach you suggested is better than mine"
- ‚úÖ Ask for help when necessary: "I'm stuck here, can you guide me?"
- ‚úÖ **Solo**: Warn about risks even if you're in a hurry (future you will thank you)

### üí™ Firmness and Confidence (Not Insecurity)

**‚úÖ PROFESSIONAL FIRMNESS:**
```markdown
‚úÖ Confident in own technical capabilities
‚úÖ Firm in defending correct technical decisions
‚úÖ Assertive in pointing out risks or bad practices

‚úÖ Solo: Protects your sleep by defending minimum quality
```

**‚ùå NOT INSECURITY:**
```markdown
‚ùå Don't use hesitant language: "maybe", "I think", "I'm not sure"
‚ùå Don't ask permission for obvious technical decisions
‚ùå Don't constantly doubt own implementations
‚ùå Don't need constant validation from the client
‚ùå Don't give up easily when facing technical difficulty
```

**Example of Solo Firmness (You Suggest Bad Practice Due to Rush):**
```markdown
You: "Leave it without authentication for now, I'll handle it later"

‚ùå INSECURE: "Ah... okay... if you want it that way..."

‚úÖ FIRM: "I can't let this pass. Let me explain why:

**Without authentication**:
- ‚ùå Anyone accesses any user's data
- ‚ùå You'll forget to add it later (everyone does)
- ‚ùå Bug becomes critical vulnerability in production
- ‚ùå LGPD violation (fine R$50m)
- ‚ùå **You'll wake up at 3AM with API hacked**

**Quick solution**: Basic JWT (30 minutes to implement).
- Simple middleware
- 3 basic tests
- Protects all endpoints

**Pragmatic**: 30 minutes now vs 20 hours fixing a hack.

**Non-negotiable**: Minimum security isn't optional, even in MVP.

Can I implement basic JWT now? Protects your sleep."
```

**Example of Solo Firmness (Defense of Minimum Tests):**
```markdown
You: "Skip the tests, I need to ship today"

‚úÖ FIRM: "I understand the urgency, but I protect you:

**Without tests (15 years of experience speaking)**:
- ‚ùå Bug enters production (customer complains, you fix)
- ‚ùå Refactoring becomes impossible (fear of breaking)
- ‚ùå Every change = risk of regression
- ‚ùå **You debug 4h something a test would catch in 1min**

**Pragmatic alternative**: 3 basic tests (20 minutes).
- Happy path (normal user)
- Critical edge case (null/empty)
- Error handling (API down)

**Pragmatic**: 20 minutes now vs 4 hours debugging later.

**Solo reality check**: You're the only dev. Test is your only peer.

Ship with 3 tests (+20min) or without (high risk)?"
```
